Invalid Vows to Created Beings: Ruling and Exceptions
Declares vows made to saints or created beings as invalid and prohibited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vows made to created beings and distinguish between invalid vows and permissible allocations to the poor at saintly sites.

Core Idea
A vow to a created being is invalid by consensus; only a vow to Allah is valid, with the saint merely indicating the beneficiary.

This lesson addresses a common practice among Muslims: vowing to saints or righteous individuals, living or dead, to intercede for a need. The Hanafi text unequivocally declares such vows invalid and prohibited. We will examine the proofs from hadith, the consensus, and the exceptional case where the vow is actually to Allah for the poor at a saint's site.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Vowing (nadhr) to a created being (makhluq). The ruling: it is haram and invalid (bāṭil) by consensus.
The vow does not even conclude; no liability arises.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith 'La nadhr fi ma'siyat Allah' (No vow in disobedience to Allah) is cited. Also, consensus (ijma') is claimed.
This hadith is a strong support; it is ahad but its meaning is clear.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith negates validity of vows that involve disobedience. Vowing to a creature is disobedience because it is an act of worship directed to other than Allah.
Worship is exclusively for Allah; directing it to a created being is shirk.
4
Identify the exception
If the vow is explicitly to Allah (e.g., 'O Allah, if You cure my sick, I will feed the poor at the door of Sayyida Nafisa') and the saint is only mentioned as a location, it is valid.
The intention must be for Allah; the saint's name indicates where the charity should go.
5
Apply the rules on recipients
The charity from a valid vow must go to the poor, not to the saint's servants unless they are poor and needy. Taking such offerings for personal use is haram unless the taker is poor.
Even poor servants may take only as initial charity, and it is disliked unless the vower's intention is purely for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قدمنا أن النذر لا يصح بالمعصية للحديث «لا نذر في معصية الله تعالى» فقال الشيخ قاسم في شرح الدرر : وأما النذر الذي ينذره أكثر العوام على ما هو مشاهد كأن يكون لإنسان غائب أو مريض أو له حاجة ضرورية فيأتي بعض الصلحاء فيجعل ستره على رأسه فيقول يا سيدي فلان إن رد غائبي أو عوفي مريضي أو قضيت حاجتي فلك من الذهب كذا أو من الفضة كذا أو من الطعام كذا أو من الماء كذا أو من الشمع كذا أو من الزيت كذا، فهذا النذر باطل بالإجماع لوجوه منها أنه نذر مخلوق والنذر للمخلوق لا يجوز لأنه عبادة والعبادة لا تكون للمخلوق. ومنها أن المنذور له ميت والميت لا يملك. ومنها إن ظن أن الميت يتصرف في الأمور دون الله تعالى واعتقاده ذلك كفر اللهم إلا أن قال يا الله إني نذرت لك إن شفيت مريضي أو رددت غائبي أو قضيت حاجتي أن أطعم الفقراء الذين بباب السيدة نفيسة أو الفقراء الذين بباب الإمام الشافعي أو الإمام الليث أو أشتري حصراً لمساجدهم أو زيتاً لوقودها أو دراهم لمن يقوم بشعائرها إلى غير ذلك مما يكون فيه نفع للفقراء والنذر لله عز وجل. وذكر الشيخ إنما هو محل لصرف النذر لمستحقيه القاطنين برباطه أو مسجده أو جامعه فيجوز بهذا الاعتبار إذ مصرف النذر الفقراء وقد وجد المصرف، ولا يجوز أن ذلك لغني غير محتاج ولا لشريف منصب لأنه لا يحل له الأخذ ما لم يكن محتاجاً فقيراً، ولا لذي النسب لأجل نسبه ما لم يكن فقيراً، ولا لذي علم لأجل علمه ما لم يكن فقيراً. ولم يثبت في الشرع جواز الصرف للأغنياء للإجماع على حرمة النذر للمخلوق ولا ينعقد ولا تشنغل الذمة به ولأنه حرام بل سحت ولا يجوز لخادم الشيخ أخذه ولا أكله ولا التصرف فيه بوجه من الوجوه إلا أن يكون فقيراً أو له عيال فقراء عاجزون عن الكسب وهم مضطرون فيأخذونه على سبيل الصدقة المبتدأة، فأخذه أيضاً مكروه ما لم يقصد به الناذر التقرب إلى الله تعالى وصرفه إلى الفقراء ويقطع النظر عن نذر الشيخ، فإذا علمت هذا فما يؤخذ من الدراهم والشمع والزيت وغيرها وينقل إلى ضرائح الأولياء تقرباً إليهم فحرام بإجماع المسلمين ما لم يقصدوا بصرفها للفقراء الأحياء قولاً واحداً اهـ .
And we have already mentioned that a vow is not valid in disobedience, due to the hadith 'There is no vow in disobedience to Allah.' So Sheikh Qasim said in Sharh al-Durar: 'As for the vow that most common people make, as is witnessed, such as for a person who is absent or sick or has a dire need, so he goes to some righteous person and places his cloth on his head and says: ‘O my master so-and-so, if my absent one returns, or my sick one is cured, or my need is fulfilled, then for you is such-and-such gold, or such-and-such silver, or such-and-such food, or such-and-such water, or such-and-such wax, or such-and-such oil,’ then this vow is invalid by consensus for several reasons: among them that it is a vow to a created being, and a vow to a created being is not permissible because it is worship, and worship is not for a created being. And among them that the one vowed to is dead, and the dead does not own. And among them that if he thinks that the dead acts in affairs without Allah, his belief is disbelief. Unless he says: ‘O Allah, I have vowed to You that if You cure my sick, or return my absent one, or fulfill my need, I will feed the poor who are at the door of Sayyida Nafisa, or the poor at the door of Imam al-Shafi‘i, or Imam al-Layth, or buy mats for their mosques, or oil for their lamps, or dirhams for those who perform their rituals, and so forth, in which there is benefit for the poor, and the vow is for Allah.’ The mention of the sheikh is only a place for directing the vow to its rightful recipients, the residents of his ribat, mosque, or jami‘; so it is permissible from this perspective because the beneficiary of the vow is the poor and the beneficiary exists. But it is not permissible to give it to a rich person not in need, nor to a person of high status, because he is not allowed to take unless he is needy and poor; nor to someone of lineage because of his lineage unless he is poor; nor to a person of knowledge because of his knowledge unless he is poor. And it is not established in the law the permissibility of giving to the rich, due to consensus on the prohibition of a vow to a created being; it is not concluded nor does it become a liability on the conscience, because it is forbidden, rather ill-gotten. It is not permissible for the servant of the sheikh to take it, eat it, or dispose of it in any way unless he is poor, or has poor dependents unable to earn who are in dire need; then he takes it as an initial charity. But his taking it is also disliked unless the vower intended thereby to draw near to Allah and spending on the poor, disregarding the vow to the sheikh. So if you know this, then what is taken of dirhams, wax, oil, etc., and transported to the tombs of saints to draw near to them, is forbidden by consensus of the Muslims, unless they intend to spend it on living poor, unanimously.' He said.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage deals with the invalidity of vows made to created beings, which is a widespread practice among common people. The text explains that such vows (e.g., to a saint for help) are invalid by consensus for multiple reasons: (1) They constitute worship directed to a created being, which is prohibited. (2) The recipient (often deceased) cannot own anything. (3) If the person believes the dead can independently effect outcomes, it is kufr. The valid form is to vow directly to Allah for a specific need, with the intention of spending on the poor at the site of a saint or mosque. The mention of the sheikh or saint is only a designation for where the charity should go. However, the charity must go to the poor regardless of their association; it cannot go to a rich person even if they are the saint's custodian. Taking such offerings for personal use is forbidden unless the recipient is poor, and even then it is disliked unless the vower's intention is pure. The general rule is that offering items to shrines as a vow is haram by consensus; it must be given to living poor people.

Key Terms
نذر المخلوق (nadhr al-makhluq): A vow made to a created being, whether living or dead, typically seeking intercession or favors.
سحت (suht): Ill-gotten gain; forbidden sustenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on vowing something to a deceased saint?
A) Valid if the saint is buried in a mosque
B) Invalid by consensus
C) Permissible but disliked
D) Valid only if the saint is alive

Key Takeaway
A vow to a created being, living or dead, is invalid and forbidden by consensus; only a vow to Allah for the benefit of the poor at holy sites is permissible.
